was reading an interesting article the other day about menswear. For many of us, when we started work, we dressed in a certain way because we needed to. One would wear a suit because it was required in the office. A tie was mandatory for meetings. Shoes were typically black and discreet. \\n\\nWith the disruption to modes of working and dress codes globally, this perspective has shifted. More and more people now wear something because they WANT to. There's more thought and enjoyment into choosing each garment. One wears a blazer, slips on a pair of brogues or carries a briefcase because one enjoys the craft and elegance behind it, not because anyone forces one to do so. \\n\\nThis pair of suede oxfords represents a perfect midway on the formality spectrum for me. Something that may seem a touch too formal with jeans and a tee or too casual with a worsted wool suit. But in this setting, with dusty orange socks and heavy olive linen trousers, it feels just right. was reading an interesting article the other day about menswear. For many of us, when we started work, we dressed in a certain way because we needed to. One would wear a suit because it was required in the office. A tie was mandatory for meetings. Shoes were typically black and discreet. \\n\\nWith the disruption to modes of working and dress codes globally, this perspective has shifted. More and more people now wear something because they WANT to. There's more thought and enjoyment into choosing each garment. One wears a blazer, slips on a pair of brogues or carries a briefcase because one enjoys the craft and elegance behind it, not because anyone forces one to do so. \\n\\nThis pair of suede oxfords represents a perfect midway on the formality spectrum for me. Something that may seem a touch too formal with jeans and a tee or too casual with a worsted wool suit. But in this setting, with dusty orange socks and heavy olive linen trousers, it feels just right. say it came together rather harmoniously! \\n\\nThere was *some* thought put into the textures though: smooth calf for the toe to allow a nice shine, tougher scotch grain for the vamp to minimise obvious creases and suede for the tongue to ensure a nice comfortable feel around the foot as it slid into the shoe. I even had plans to replicate this in blue.
